994bafd0-d179-4b1a-ab29-3b01ceb0d500	Capillary Sampling 	 Author/Originator: Prabhjot Batth (Nurse Practitioner)\nApproved by: Sandeep Sarkar (Medical Physician) in June 2023.\nImplementation Date: June 2023\nRecently Reviewed by: Prabhjot Batth\nBetween 01/2024-09/2025- Policies were purchased from QCS.\nNew Version after review: V1.2\nReview date: 10/09/2025\n\n\n\n\n	Blood Tests	active	1.2	<p><strong>Introduction</strong></p><p>Capillary blood sampling is a minimally invasive method for obtaining blood from the body, typically used for point-of-care testing, small-volume laboratory tests, or when venous access is difficult.</p><ul><li>In adults, the finger is the preferred site.</li><li>In neonates and infants, heel puncture is generally used, preserving venous access for future procedures.</li></ul><p>Capillary sampling is widely used due to its accessibility, low patient discomfort, and rapid collection. Proper technique ensures accuracy and reduces the risk of complications.</p><p>&nbsp;</p><p><strong>About Lancets</strong></p><ul><li>Lancets should be slightly shorter than the estimated penetration depth, as tissue compression increases actual puncture depth.</li><li>Pain increases with lancet depth; thicker lancets are slightly more painful.</li><li>Lancet lengths typically range from 0.85 mm (neonates) to 2.2 mm (adults). Maximum recommended depth for finger-prick in adults is 2.4 mm.</li></ul><p>&nbsp;</p><p><strong>Equipment</strong></p><ul><li>Sterile lancet</li><li>Capillary sampling machine or micro collection tubes/strips</li><li>Gauze or cotton swabs</li><li>Disposable kidney tray</li><li>Personal protective equipment (PPE)  gloves, apron, mask if required</li><li>Sample collection devices</li><li>Consent forms (verbal consent acceptable in routine practice)</li><li>Ensure capillary sampling machines undergo periodic quality control checks.</li></ul><p>&nbsp;</p><p><strong>Consent</strong></p><ul><li>Obtain verbal consent prior to the procedure.</li><li>Explain the procedure, purpose, and reassure the patient regarding minimal discomfort and blood volume.</li></ul><p>&nbsp;</p><p><strong>Environment</strong></p><ul><li>Maintain patient privacy, dignity, and comfort during the procedure.</li><li>Ensure proper lighting and ergonomics for both patient and phlebotomist.</li></ul><p>&nbsp;</p><p><strong>Procedure Steps</strong></p><ol><li>Perform hand hygiene and put on PPE.</li><li>Use gloves during all blood collection procedures, changing between patients.</li><li>Identify the patient using two forms of identification.</li><li>Reassure the patient that only the minimum blood required will be collected.</li><li>Position the patient comfortably, ensuring the limb is supported.</li><li>Limit capillary punctures to a maximum of two attempts per site; notify a manager if unsuccessful.</li><li>Clean the puncture site with an appropriate antiseptic and allow to air dry.</li><li>Puncture the skin with a single, deliberate motion.</li><li>Wipe away the first drop of blood to avoid contamination.</li><li>Avoid excessive squeezing, which can dilute the sample with tissue fluid.</li><li>Apply firm pressure after collection to stop bleeding.</li></ol><p>&nbsp;</p><p>&nbsp;</p><p><strong>Order of Draw</strong></p><ul><li>For capillary samples: hematology specimens first, followed by chemistry and blood bank specimens.</li><li>This is essential to minimise platelet clumping and contamination.</li><li>For multiple specimens, consider venepuncture for more accurate results.</li></ul><p>&nbsp;</p><p><strong>Complications</strong></p><p>Potential complications include:</p><ul><li>Nerve damage (especially in neonates)</li><li>Hematoma or loss of venous access</li><li>Scarring or tissue necrosis (rare)</li><li>Skin breakdown from repeated adhesive use</li></ul><p><strong>Prevention:</strong> Proper technique, careful site selection, and post-procedure observation.</p><p>&nbsp;</p><p>&nbsp;</p><p><strong>Safe Disposal</strong></p><ul><li>Dispose of lancets in sharps containers immediately.</li><li>Gloves and single-use items must be disposed of according to biohazard waste protocols.</li><li>Clean contaminated surfaces with appropriate disinfectant.</li><li>Accidental sharps injury: wash area with soap and water, encourage bleeding, and report to line manager immediately.</li></ul><p>&nbsp;</p><p><strong>Follow-Up Care</strong></p><p><strong>&nbsp;</strong></p><p><strong>Two key steps:</strong></p><ol><li><strong>Patient care:</strong></li></ol><p>-Provide reassurance, check the puncture site, and ensure patient comfort.</p><ol><li><strong>Data entry / specimen labeling:</strong></li></ol><p>-Record:</p><ul><li class="ql-indent-2">Date and time of collection</li><li class="ql-indent-2">Patient name and ID number</li><li class="ql-indent-2">Tests requested</li><li class="ql-indent-2">Method of collection (capillary or venepuncture)</li><li class="ql-indent-2">Phlebotomists name and signature</li></ul><p>&nbsp;</p><p><strong>References:</strong></p><p><strong>&nbsp;</strong></p><ol><li>World Health Organization. <em>WHO Guidelines on Drawing Blood: Best Practices in Phlebotomy</em>. Geneva: WHO, 2010. NCBI Bookshelf</li><li>NHS Scotland (2023). <em>Capillary Blood Sampling  Clinical Guidelines</em>. </li><li>University of Florida Health (2023). <em>Capillary Blood Collection Procedure</em>. Link</li><li>Krleza, JL, Dorotic, A, Grzunov, A, Maradin, M. <em>Capillary blood sampling: national recommendations</em>, Croatian Society of Medical Biochemistry, 2015; 25(3): 335358.</li></ol><p>&nbsp;</p><p><strong>Professional Enhancements</strong></p><ul><li>Aligned with latest NHS and WHO guidance.</li><li>Included patient safety, consent, and post-procedure care.</li><li>Updated terminology: capillary puncture instead of finger-stick, clarified order of draw.</li><li>Added risk management and sharps safety procedures.</li><li>Structured as a policy/procedure document suitable for clinical governance and staff training.</li></ul><p>&nbsp;</p><p>&nbsp;</p><p><br></p><p><br></p><p><br></p><p><br></p><p><br></p><p><br></p><p><br></p><p><br></p><p><br></p><p><br></p><p><br></p><p><br></p><p><br></p><p><br></p><p><br></p><p><br></p><p><br></p><p><br></p><p><br></p><p><br></p><p><br></p>	d931efb6-4f85-4d80-91a8-be3420c2f648	2025-09-26 13:04:17.587342+00	2025-09-26 13:04:17.587342+00
ebe1cf20-e471-4400-92dc-a6fd78e3e11c	Whistleblowing 	Policy Author/Originator: Prabhjot Batth (Nurse Practitioner) and Bernadette OShea (Nurse Practitioner)\nApproved by: Sandeep Sarkar (Medical Physician), October 2023\nImplementation Date: October 2023\nAnnual Review/Update: QCS policies purchased from January 2024 to September 2025\nLatest Update: Policy updated by Prabhjot Batth on 26 September 2025	Safety Protocols	active	1.2	<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;                             &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</p><h2><strong>Introduction</strong></h2><p>Whistleblowing is the disclosure of information relating to suspected wrongdoing or dangers at work. The term <em>whistleblower</em> refers to someone who makes a <em>qualifying disclosure</em> about a genuine concern at work. Workers who suffer detriment or dismissal as a result of raising such concerns may have employment protections under the Employment Rights Act 1996, as amended by the Public Interest Disclosure Act 1998 (PIDA).</p><p><br></p><h2><strong>Purpose</strong></h2><p>This policy aims to:</p><ul><li>Ensure all staff understand the importance of raising concerns (speaking up or whistleblowing).</li><li>Apply to all employees, officers, consultants, contractors, volunteers, interns, casual workers, and agency workers.</li><li>Encourage staff to report suspected wrongdoing promptly, with confidentiality and assurance of appropriate investigation.</li><li>Provide clear guidance for raising concerns.</li><li>Reassure staff that they can raise genuine concerns without fear of reprisals, even if mistaken.</li><li>Clarify that personal grievances should follow the Grievance Policy and Procedure.</li><li>Support Batth Medicals Limited in meeting Key Lines of Enquiry (KLOEs) and Quality Statements.</li><li><br></li></ul><h2><strong>Scope</strong></h2><p><strong>Roles affected:</strong></p><ul><li>All staff, including NHS staff, temporary agency staff, and persons on training courses</li></ul><p><strong>Service Users affected:</strong></p><ul><li>All service users</li></ul><p><strong>Stakeholders affected:</strong></p><ul><li>Commissioners</li><li>Local Authorities</li><li>Care Quality Commission (CQC).</li><li><br></li></ul><h2><strong>Relevant Legislation</strong></h2><ul><li>Criminal Justice and Courts Act 2015</li><li>Enterprise and Regulatory Reform Act 2013</li><li>Care Act 2014</li><li>Employment Rights Act 1996</li><li>Public Interest Disclosure Act 1998</li><li>Health and Social Care Act 2008 (Regulated Activities) (Amendment) Regulations 2012.</li></ul><p><br></p><h2><strong>Policy Statement</strong></h2><ul><li>Batth Medicals Limited is committed to honesty, openness, and decency in all activities, prioritizing service user safety. Failure to raise concerns can have serious consequences for the organisation, staff, and service users.</li><li>The organisation encourages a culture of open communication and recognises staff are often the first to notice wrongdoing. Staff may fear disloyalty, harassment, or job loss; Batth Medicals Limited does <strong>not tolerate ill-treatment</strong> of whistleblowers.</li><li>Whistleblowers raising genuine concerns will <strong>not face termination or reprisals</strong>, including changes to hours or working patterns.</li><li>The organisation follows both the law on whistleblowing and best practice guidance from the NHS and regulatory bodies such as the CQC.</li></ul><p><br></p><h2><strong>Procedure</strong></h2><h3><strong>Raising Concerns</strong></h3><ol><li><strong>Step 1  Line Manager:</strong></li></ol><ul><li class="ql-indent-1">Staff should ideally raise concerns first with their line manager, verbally or in writing.</li><li class="ql-indent-1">Concerns should be raised promptly.</li><li class="ql-indent-1">Confidentiality will be maintained unless disclosure is required, e.g., safeguarding matters.</li></ul><ol><li><strong>Step 2  Registered Manager:</strong></li></ol><ul><li class="ql-indent-1">If the concern involves the line manager or is unresolved, escalate to the Registered Manager.</li></ul><ol><li><strong>Step 3  External Reporting:</strong></li></ol><ul><li class="ql-indent-1">If unresolved internally, concerns may be reported to the CQC.</li><li><br></li></ul><h3><strong>Protection and Support</strong></h3><ul><li>Whistleblowers must not face dismissal, disciplinary action, or threats.</li><li>If detrimental treatment occurs, inform the Registered Manager or use the Grievance Procedure.</li><li>Threats or retaliation against whistleblowers may lead to disciplinary action.</li><li>Staff may seek independent advice from:</li><li class="ql-indent-1">Whistleblowing Helpline for NHS and Social Care</li><li class="ql-indent-1">Public Concern at Work (whistleblowing charity).</li><li><br></li></ul><h3><strong>Investigation</strong></h3><ul><li>The Registered Manager may arrange a meeting; staff may bring a colleague or union representative.</li><li>Investigations may involve other agencies if required, including Adult Social Services or Police for criminal activity.</li><li>Outcomes may not always meet the whistleblowers expectations but will be handled fairly.</li></ul><p><br></p><h3><strong>Responsibilities</strong></h3><ul><li><strong>Registered Manager:</strong> Responsible for managing concerns.</li><li><strong>Escalation:</strong> If concerns involve the Registered Manager or senior staff, escalate to the senior regulated authority.</li></ul><p><br></p><h3><strong>Protected Disclosures &amp; Safeguarding</strong></h3><ul><li>Follow Batth Medicals Ltd safeguarding policies.</li><li>If a safeguarding concern involves management, refer to the Local Social Services Adult Protection Team.</li></ul><p><br></p><h3><strong>Timescales</strong></h3><ul><li>Concerns acknowledged promptly; investigating officer assigned with contact and estimated timeline.</li><li>Feedback to whistleblower provided where possible.</li><li>Records maintained according to best practice.</li></ul><p><br></p><h3><strong>False or Malicious Allegations</strong></h3><ul><li>Malicious or vexatious allegations may lead to disciplinary action.</li><li>Genuine concerns, even if mistaken, will not result in disciplinary action if the correct procedure is followed.</li></ul><p><br></p><h3><strong>Bullying and Harassment of Whistleblowers</strong></h3><ul><li>Batth Medicals Limited will proactively prevent bullying or harassment.</li><li>Steps include:</li><li class="ql-indent-1">Adhering to the Whistleblowing Policy</li><li class="ql-indent-1">Embedding openness and transparency</li><li class="ql-indent-1">Communicating policy and providing training</li><li class="ql-indent-1">Acting against staff who bully or harass whistleblowers.</li><li><br></li></ul><h3><strong>Employment Contracts &amp; Confidentiality</strong></h3><ul><li>Whistleblowers protected by PIDA; contracts will not prevent claims.</li><li>Legal or HR advice will be sought if necessary.</li></ul><p><br></p><h3><strong>Monitoring, Review, Continuous Improvement</strong></h3><ul><li>Continuous improvement encouraged through feedback, audits, and quality assurance.</li><li>Barriers to speaking up are actively addressed.</li></ul><p><br></p><h3><strong>External Disclosures</strong></h3><ul><li>Internal reporting is preferred; external reporting is only in specific circumstances.</li><li>Staff should seek advice before contacting media or external parties.</li></ul><p><br></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><br></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(0, 112, 192);">How to Raise Concerns (Flowchart)</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">&nbsp;&nbsp;</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">Start  Do you have a genuine concern about risk, malpractice, or wrongdoing at work?&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">Yes  </span><strong style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">Step 1: Raise with Line Manager</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Verbally or in writing</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Confidential where possible</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Line Manager informs if confidentiality cannot be maintained.</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><strong style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">Concern resolved?</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </strong><span style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">Yes  End / Matter Resolved</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</strong><span style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);"> No</span><strong style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">  Step 2: Escalate to Registered Manager.</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Concern resolved?</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">&nbsp;</strong><span style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);"> Yes  End / Matter Resolved</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">&nbsp; No</span><strong style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">  Step 3: Report externally (e.g., CQC).</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">&nbsp;</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">&nbsp;Investigation &amp; Outcome</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Investigation conducted by Registered Manager or external authority if needed.</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Staff may bring a colleague or union representative.</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Feedback provided where possible.</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(53, 53, 53);">Support &amp; 11719127-2194-494b-9ef7-da61e57b0f55	Dignity & Respect	Policy Author/Originator: Prabhjot Batth (Nurse Practitioner) and Bernadette OShea (Nurse Practitioner)\nApproved by: Sandeep Sarkar (Medical Physician), July 2023\nImplementation Date: October 2023\nAnnual Review/Update: QCS policies purchased from January 2024 to September 2025\nLatest Update: Policy updated by Prabhjot Batth in September 2025\n\n	Patient Care	active	1.2	<p><strong>Policy Statement</strong></p><p><strong>&nbsp;</strong></p><p>Batth Medicals Ltd (BML) is committed to creating and maintaining a workplace where every individual is treated with dignity, fairness, and respect. This applies to all staff, patients, service users, contractors, and visitors. BML has a zero-tolerance approach to discrimination, harassment, bullying, and victimisation in any form.</p><p><br></p><p><strong>Aims</strong></p><p>This policy aims to:</p><ul><li>Promote a working environment where employees, associates, and service users are treated with respect and dignity.</li><li>Prevent harassment, bullying, and unlawful discrimination.</li><li>Provide a clear process for resolving issues through informal resolution, mediation, or formal procedures.</li><li>Ensure complaints are handled fairly, consistently, and promptly.</li></ul><p><br></p><p><strong>Purpose and Scope</strong></p><ul><li>Protect employees and service users from harassment and bullying while on BML premises or during work-related activities.</li><li>Complaints outside the scope of this policy (e.g., general employment matters) are addressed under the Grievance Policy.</li><li>Contractors or temporary staff suspected of harassment or bullying may have their contract terminated without recourse to BML policies.</li><li>This policy does not cover:</li><li>&nbsp;Complaints raised on behalf of another employee.</li><li>Whistleblowing issues (covered under the Whistleblowing Policy).</li><li>Complaints relating to groups of employees.</li></ul><p><br></p><p><strong>Principles</strong></p><p>To maintain a respectful working environment, BML upholds the following principles:</p><ul><li>All employees have the right to be treated with dignity, fairness, and without unlawful discrimination.</li><li>Complaints will be addressed promptly and without unreasonable delay.</li><li>Employees are encouraged to attempt informal resolution where appropriate.</li><li>Malicious, frivolous, or vexatious complaints may lead to disciplinary action.</li><li>Managers make decisions on the balance of probabilities based on available evidence.</li><li>Staff are expected to treat colleagues in accordance with BMLs core values, Code of Conduct, Equality &amp; Diversity Policy, and Competency Framework.</li><li>Offense caused unintentionally due to lack of awareness may result in awareness training; deliberate misconduct will lead to disciplinary action.</li><li>All complaints are assumed to be raised in good faith.</li></ul><p>&nbsp;</p><p><strong>Outcome</strong></p><p>This policy ensures:</p><ul><li>Employees know how to raise dignity-related complaints and trust that they will be handled appropriately.</li><li>Managers understand the procedures to manage complaints effectively.</li><li>Issues are resolved informally where possible, minimizing recourse to formal procedures.</li></ul><p><br></p><p><strong>Monitoring and Review</strong></p><ul><li>BML managers, clinical directors, and HR monitor compliance with this policy.</li><li>Formal review occurs if there are legislative changes or business needs that require updates.</li></ul><p><br></p><p><strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</strong><strong style="color: rgb(0, 112, 192);">Dignity at Work Procedure</strong></p><p><strong>1. Informal Stage</strong></p><ul><li>Employees should first attempt to resolve concerns directly with the individual(s) involved.</li><li>If unable, escalate to the line manager or, if the concern involves the line manager, to the countersigning manager. HR or the Board of Directors can provide advice.</li><li>Steps for informal resolution:</li></ul><ol><li class="ql-indent-1">Ask for details of the alleged behaviour.</li><li class="ql-indent-1">Apologize if appropriate.</li><li class="ql-indent-1">Explain your viewpoint calmly without becoming defensive.</li><li class="ql-indent-1">Consider training, mediation, or conciliation.</li></ol><ul><li>Keep a note of discussions and agreed actions.</li></ul><p><br></p><p><strong>2. Formal Stage</strong></p><p><strong>Raising a Complaint</strong></p><ul><li>Complaints must be submitted in writing to the line manager with copies to HR and the Board of Directors.</li><li>If the complaint concerns the line manager, submit to the countersigning manager.</li><li>Include in writing:</li></ul><p>v&nbsp;Detailed chronology of events</p><p>v&nbsp;Attempts at informal resolution</p><p>v&nbsp;Desired outcome</p><p><br></p><p><strong>Initial Assessment</strong></p><ul><li>BML may conduct an initial assessment to determine if the complaint is genuine and whether informal resolution might be sufficient.</li><li>The Dignity at Work Manager is appointed to ensure procedural fairness.</li></ul><p><br></p><p><strong>Investigation</strong></p><ul><li>The Investigator will gather evidence, interview the complainant, the subject of the complaint, and witnesses.</li><li>Investigators may be supported by HR or Board of Directors.</li><li>Upon completion, a report will summarize findings, evidence, and any conflicting information.</li></ul><p><br></p><p><strong>Decision</strong></p><ul><li>The <strong>Dignity at Work Manager</strong> will hold a decision meeting with the complainant (with right to accompaniment).</li><li>A decision letter will include:</li><li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Outcome (fully, partly, or not upheld</li><li>Investigation summary</li><li>&nbsp;Further actions</li><li>Appeal procedure</li></ul><p><br></p><p><strong>Disciplinary Considerations</strong></p><ul><li>If warranted, matters may proceed under the Disciplinary Policy, leveraging the investigation findings.</li></ul><p><br></p><p><strong>3. Appeal</strong></p><ul><li>Appeals must be submitted within 10 working days of the decision letter.</li><li>Appeals should include grounds for appeal and any supporting documentation.</li><li>The Appeal Manager will assess procedural adherence, new evidence, and reasonableness of the decision.</li><li>Appeal outcomes:</li><li>&nbsp;Fully upheld (no further action)</li><li>Partially upheld (further action may be taken)</li><li>Dismissed (original decision stands)</li></ul><p><br></p><p><strong>Timescales</strong></p><ul><li>Complaints should be resolved promptly to protect both the complainant and the subject of the complaint.</li></ul><p><br></p><p><strong>Mediation</strong></p><ul><li>Mediation may be used as a constructive resolution method.</li><li>Requires mutual agreement and is typically conducted by trained external mediators</li></ul><p><br></p><p><strong>Confidentiality</strong></p><ul><li>Strict confidentiality must be maintained by all participants.</li><li>Documents related to complaints should be marked <strong></strong>Restricted.</li></ul><p><br></p><p><strong>Professional Enhancements Made</strong></p><ol><li>Structured headings for clarity and readability.</li><li>Modern HR language and legal terminology added (e.g., balance of probabilities, zero-tolerance approach).</li><li>Formalized complaint, investigation, decision, and appeal steps.</li><li>Emphasized alignment with Code of Conduct, Equality &amp; Diversity, and Competency Framework.</li><li>Incorporated clarity on informal resolution, mediation, and confidentiality.</li><li>Ensured policy compliance with current employment law and best practice standards</li></ol><p><br></p><p><br></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>References / Legislation and Guidance</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify">1.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Employment Rights Act 1996  Protection of employees and fair treatment at work.</p><p 6f13bbd9-824d-4d39-b292-25a455cc6a36	Consent	Policy Author/Originator: Prabhjot Batth (Nurse Practitioner) and Bernadette OShea (Nurse Practitioner)\nApproved by: Sandeep Sarkar (Medical Physician) March 2023\nImplementation Date: October 2023\nAnnual Review/Update: QCS policies purchased from January 2024 to September 2025\nLatest Update: Policy updated by Prabhjot Batth in September 2025.\n\n	Patient Care	active	1.2	<p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">1. Policy Statement</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">Batth Medicals Ltd (BML) is committed to ensuring that valid consent is obtained for all examinations, procedures, or treatments. All staff involved in care provision must respect patients rights, follow legal and ethical frameworks, and ensure informed decision-making. This policy applies to all staff, including permanent, temporary, and contractor roles acting for or on behalf of BML.</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">2. Scope</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">This policy applies to:</span></p><ul><li class="ql-align-justify">All clinical and non-clinical staff involved in patient care.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Any procedure requiring consent, including blood tests, minor procedures, and clinical interventions.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Patients, service users, and vulnerable adults under the care of BML.</li></ul><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">3. Introduction</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">Patients and service users have a fundamental legal and ethical right to determine what happens to their own bodies. Obtaining valid consent is central to all healthcare activities and reflects professional courtesy, patient autonomy, and safety.</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">Consent is not a one-time event but a continuous process of information provision, discussion, and decision-making.</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">4. Definition of Consent</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">Consent is the agreement by a patient or service user for a healthcare professional to provide care or treatment.</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">For consent to be valid, the patient must:</span></p><ul><li class="ql-align-justify">Have capacity to make the decision.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Receive sufficient, relevant information.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Make the decision voluntarily, without duress or undue influence.</li></ul><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">Types of Consent:</strong></p><ol><li class="ql-align-justify"><strong>Non-verbal Consent:</strong> e.g., offering an arm for a blood pressure check.</li><li class="ql-align-justify"><strong>Verbal Consent:</strong> e.g., agreeing to a routine weight measurement.</li><li class="ql-align-justify"><strong>Written Consent:</strong> required for procedures with higher risk, such as surgical interventions.</li></ol><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">5. Aims and Objectives</strong></p><ul><li class="ql-align-justify">Ensure consent is obtained lawfully, consistently, and ethically.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Support patients to make informed decisions when they have capacity.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Ensure decisions for patients who lack capacity comply with the Mental Capacity Act 2005 (MCA).</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Promote staff awareness and adherence to legal, ethical, and professional standards regarding consent.</li></ul><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">6. Legal and Ethical Framework</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">Key legislation and guidance includes:</span></p><ul><li class="ql-align-justify"><strong>Mental Capacity Act 2005</strong>  statutory framework for patients who lack capacity.</li><li class="ql-align-justify"><strong>Human Rights Act 1998</strong>  right to bodily integrity and autonomy.</li><li class="ql-align-justify"><strong>Department of Health Reference Guide to Consent (2nd Edition, 2009)</strong></li><li class="ql-align-justify"><strong>NHS Consent to Treatment Guidance</strong></li></ul><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">Informed Consent Purposes:</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify">   <strong style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">Purpose</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"> <strong style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">Description</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify">    <span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">Legal:</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"> <span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">Protects patients from assault or unwanted interventions.</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify">   <span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">Ethical:</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"> <span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">Ensures patient autonomy and decisions aligned with their values.</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify">   <span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">Administrative</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"> <span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">:Documents that consent has been obtained for compliance and audit purposes.</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify">  <span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">7. When Consent Is Not Required</strong></p><ul><li class="ql-align-justify">Emergency treatment to save life or prevent serious harm, where the patient is incapacitated.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Treatment may proceed without consent if it is in the patients best interests and cannot wait.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Explanation should be provided once the patient regains capacity.</li></ul><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">8. Valid Consent Criteria</strong></p><ul><li class="ql-align-justify"><strong>Voluntary:</strong> Decision made without pressure.</li><li class="ql-align-justify"><strong>Informed:</strong> Patient understands risks, benefits, alternatives, and consequences of refusal.</li><li class="ql-align-justify"><strong>Capacity:</strong> Patient can comprehend, retain, weigh information, and communicate a decision.</li></ul><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">&nbsp;</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">Capacity Assessment:</strong></p><ul><li class="ql-align-justify">Based on ability to make a specific decision at the time.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Follow MCA 2005 Code of Practice: understand, retain, weigh, communicate.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">If lacking capacity, treatment may be given in the patients best interests, considering advance directives.</li></ul><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">Deprivation of Liberty Safeguards (DoLS):</strong><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);"> Protects vulnerable adults in hospitals or care homes from unlawful deprivation of liberty when treatment is necessary and capacity is limited.</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">9. Staff Responsibilities</strong></p><ul><li class="ql-align-justify">Ensure consent is valid before any procedure.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Provide sufficient information in a comprehensible manner.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Document consent in patient records accurately.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Notify the duty manager if a patient lacks capacity.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Recognize that failure to obtain valid consent may result in criminal or civil liability.</li></ul><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">Director/Nominated Person for Safety &amp; Governance:</strong></p><ul><li class="ql-align-justify">Ensures staff are trained in consent processes.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Reviews policy compliance with legislation updates.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Monitors systems for auditing consent and reports compliance to the Board.</li></ul><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">10. Training</strong></p><ul><li class="ql-align-justify">All clinical staff receive training on consent during corporate induction.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Additional training provided group-based or on request.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Refresher training aligned with legislation or professional updates.</li></ul><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">11. Monitoring and Compliance</strong></p><ul><li class="ql-align-justify">Annual audits of consent compliance will be reported to directors and the clinical team.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Non-compliance or incidents related to consent will trigger <strong>review and action plans</strong>.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Audit includes adherence to legal requirements, documentation quality, and evidence of informed discussions.</li></ul><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">References</strong></p><ol><li class="ql-align-justify">NHS. <em>Consent to Treatment</em>. <a href="https://www.nhs.uk/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">https://www.nhs.uk/</a></li><li class="ql-align-justify">Hall DE, Prochazka AV, Fink AS. <em>Informed Consent for Clinical Treatment</em>. CMAJ. 2012;184(5):533540.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Berg JW, Appelbaum PS, Lidz CW, et al. <em>Informed Consent: Legal Theory and Clinical Practice</em>, 2nd ed. Oxford University Press, 2001.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Department of Health (2001). <em>Good Practice in Consent: Implementation Guide</em>.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Department of Health (2009). <em>Reference Guide to Consent for Examination or Treatment</em>, 2nd Edition.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Mental Capacity Act 2005, Code of Practice.</li></ol><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><span style="color: rgb(34, 34, 34);">&nbsp;</span></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><br></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>&nbsp;</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>&nbsp;</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>&nbsp;</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</p><p class="ql-align-justify"><br></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><br></p><p class="ql-align-justify">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</p><p class="ql-align-justify"><br></p><p><br></p>	d931efb6-4f85-4d80-91a8-be3420c2f648	2025-09-26 13:20:37.79128+00	2025-09-26 13:20:37.79128+00
5d6d0873-f65f-4484-b7e8-64f45966ba6b	Needle Stick Injury	Policy Author/Originator: Prabhjot Batth (Nurse Practitioner) and Bernadette OShea (Nurse Practitioner) with the guidance of Sandeep Sarkar (Medical Physician).\nDate: May 2023\nImplementation Date: October 2023\nAnnual Review/Update: QCS policies purchased from January 2024 to September 2025\nLatest Update: Policy updated by Prabhjot Batth in September 2025\n\n\n\n\n	Blood Tests	active	1.2	<p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>1. Policy Statement</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify">Batth Medicals Ltd (BML) is committed to maintaining a safe working environment and reducing the risk of occupational exposure to bloodborne viruses (BBVs). This policy outlines measures to prevent, manage, and report needle stick injuries (NSIs) and other sharps-related incidents<strong>.</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>&nbsp;</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>2. Scope</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify">This policy applies to:</p><ul><li class="ql-align-justify">All staff, including permanent, temporary, and contractors, involved in clinical activities or handling sharps.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Procedures involving needles, scalpels, lancets, and other sharp instruments.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Management of exposures to blood or other potentially infectious materials.</li></ul><p class="ql-align-justify">&nbsp;</p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>3. Introduction</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify">A needle stick injury occurs when a needle or other sharp instrument punctures the skin, creating a potential route for BBV transmission, including Hepatitis B (HBV), Hepatitis C (HCV), and HIV.</p><p class="ql-align-justify">Healthcare workers (HCWs) are at risk through:</p><ul><li class="ql-align-justify">Injuries with sharps (needles, blades, broken glass).</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Punctures/lacerations from contaminated materials.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Blood or bodily fluid splashes onto broken skin or mucous membranes.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Scratches or bites that break the skin.</li></ul><p class="ql-align-justify">&nbsp;</p><p class="ql-align-justify">&nbsp;</p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>4. Fluids and Tissues Posing Risk</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>&nbsp;</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>High-risk fluids:</strong></p><ul><li class="ql-align-justify">Blood (primary risk)</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Amniotic fluid, breast milk, cerebrospinal fluid</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Peritoneal, pericardial, pleural fluid</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Semen, vaginal secretions, synovial fluid</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Unfixed tissues and organs</li></ul><p class="ql-align-justify">&nbsp;</p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>Low-risk fluids:</strong></p><ul><li class="ql-align-justify">Urine, faeces, vomit, sputum (unless visibly blood-stained)</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Saliva (if blood-contaminated, e.g., dental procedures).</li></ul><p class="ql-align-justify">&nbsp;</p><p class="ql-align-justify">&nbsp;</p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>5. Risk of Transmission from BBV-Positive Source Patient.</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>&nbsp;</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify">  <strong>&nbsp;</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify">    <strong>Virus</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"> <strong>Estimated Risk per Exposure</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify">    Hepatitis B (HBeAg positive)</p><p class="ql-align-justify"> 1 in 3</p><p class="ql-align-justify">   Hepatitis C</p><p class="ql-align-justify"> 1 in 30</p><p class="ql-align-justify">   HIV</p><p class="ql-align-justify"> 1 in 300</p><p class="ql-align-justify">  <strong>&nbsp;</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>Risk factors increasing transmission:</strong></p><ul><li class="ql-align-justify">Deep or hollow-bore needle injuries</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Blood-stained needles</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Source patient not on treatment for HIV/AIDS</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Injuries involving tissue damage</li></ul><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>Note: </strong>BBVs are not transmitted through intact skin.</p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>&nbsp;</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>6. Prevention of Needle Stick Injuries</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>&nbsp;</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>6.1 Sharps Management</strong></p><ul><li class="ql-align-justify">Sharps bins must be accessible, signed, dated, and replaced when half full.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Dispose of sharps immediately after use, one at a time.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Never recap needles.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Use safety-engineered devices whenever possible.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Follow universal precautions (gloves, PPE) for all procedures.</li></ul><p class="ql-align-justify">&nbsp;</p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>6.2 Staff Responsibilities</strong></p><ol><li class="ql-align-justify"><strong>Immunisation:</strong></li></ol><p class="ql-align-justify">-&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Ensure Hepatitis B vaccination for all clinical staff.</p><p class="ql-align-justify">-&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Risk assess non-immune staff and plan accordingly.</p><ol><li class="ql-align-justify"><strong>Hygiene:</strong></li></ol><p class="ql-align-justify">-&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Wash hands before/after patient contact and glove use.</p><p class="ql-align-justify">-&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Cover cuts or breaks in skin; use waterproof dressings.</p><p class="ql-align-justify">&nbsp;</p><ol><li class="ql-align-justify"><strong>PPE and Safe Practices:</strong></li></ol><p class="ql-align-justify">-&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Wear gloves, masks, and protective clothing as needed.</p><p class="ql-align-justify">-&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Avoid open footwear in clinical areas.</p><p class="ql-align-justify">-&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Use single-use disposable injection equipment.</p><p class="ql-align-justify">&nbsp;</p><ol><li class="ql-align-justify"><strong>Decontamination and Linen Handling:</strong></li></ol><p class="ql-align-justify">-&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Clean spills immediately; disinfect surfaces.</p><p class="ql-align-justify">-&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Handle contaminated linen with gloves and leak-proof bags<strong>.</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><br></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>Documentation:</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify">-&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Record sterilisation of equipment, sharps disposal, and incidents.</p><p class="ql-align-justify"><br></p><p><strong>Reference:</strong> Health and Safety (Sharp Instruments in Healthcare) Regulations 2013; NICE Guidelines 2012.</p><p><br></p><p><br></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>7. Management of Blood Exposure Incidents</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>&nbsp;</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>7.1 Immediate Action</strong></p><ol><li class="ql-align-justify">Wash the affected area with soap and water; avoid scrubbing.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Encourage free bleeding, but do not suck the wound.</li></ol><p class="ql-align-justify">&nbsp;</p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>7.2 Reporting</strong></p><ul><li class="ql-align-justify">Notify the manager on duty immediately.</li></ul><p class="ql-align-justify">&nbsp;</p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>7.3 Risk Assessment</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>&nbsp;</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>Source patient assessment:</strong></p><ul><li class="ql-align-justify">Identify and review medical history.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Obtain consent for HIV, HBV, HCV testing if required.</li></ul><p class="ql-align-justify">&nbsp;</p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>Staff assessment:</strong></p><ul><li class="ql-align-justify">Check Hepatitis B immunisation status.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Obtain consent for serum saving if needed.</li></ul><p class="ql-align-justify">&nbsp;</p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>7.4 Consultation and Follow-Up</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>&nbsp;</strong></p><ul><li class="ql-align-justify">Refer to A&amp;E or Occupational Health.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Administer post-exposure prophylaxis (PEP) for HIV if indicated.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Provide Hepatitis B immunoglobulin (HBIG) or vaccine booster if non-immune.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Follow-up testing schedule<strong>:</strong></li><li class="ql-align-justify">  Advise staff on safe practices (e.g., abstaining from donating blood, safe sex) until results confirmed.</li></ul><p class="ql-align-justify"><br></p><p class="ql-align-justify">   <strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;Test Timing</strong></p><p class="ql-align-justify">    &nbsp;&nbsp;HCV RNA- 6 weeks post-exposure</p><p class="ql-align-justify">   &nbsp;HCV Ab &amp; HBV Ab- 12 weeks post-exposure</p><p class="ql-align-justify">   &nbsp;HBsAg, HCV Ab, HIV Ab-  24 weeks post-exposure</p><p class="ql-align-justify"><br></p><ul><li class="ql-align-justify"><br></li></ul><p class="ql-align-justify">&nbsp;</p><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>7.5 Occupational Health Department (OHD) Role</strong></p><ul><li class="ql-align-justify">Ensure testing and prophylaxis arranged.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Maintain confidential records.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Perform annual audit of all NSIs.</li><li class="ql-align-justify">Document root causes a</li></ul><p class="ql-align-justify"><strong>&nbsp;</strong></p><h2><strong>8. Documentation and Record-Keeping</strong></h2><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Record source of sharps, location, time, and witnesses.</p><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Maintain secure patient identifiers and staff records.</p><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Document all advice, interventions, and follow-up.</p><p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Ensure confidentiality in both patient and staff records.</p><p><br></p><p><br></p><p><br></p><p><br></p><p><strong>References</strong></p><ol><li class="ql-align-justify"><strong>Health and Safety Executive (1999). <em>Sharps admins will be assigned manually\n  INSERT INTO public.user_roles (user_id, role)\n  VALUES (NEW.id, 'staff');\n  \n  RETURN NEW;\nEND;\n$$;\n\n-- Create trigger for new user signup\nCREATE TRIGGER on_auth_user_created\n  AFTER INSERT ON auth.users\n  FOR EACH ROW EXECUTE FUNCTION public.handle_new_user();\n\n-- RLS Policies for profiles\nCREATE POLICY \\"Users can view their own profile\\"\n  ON public.profiles\n  FOR SELECT\n  TO authenticated\n  USING (auth.uid() = user_id);\n\nCREATE POLICY \\"Users can update their own profile\\"\n  ON public.profiles\n  FOR UPDATE\n  TO authenticated\n  USING (auth.uid() = user_id);\n\nCREATE POLICY \\"Admins can view all profiles\\"\n  ON public.profiles\n  FOR SELECT\n  TO authenticated\n  USING (public.has_role(auth.uid(), 'admin'));\n\n-- RLS Policies for user_roles\nCREATE POLICY \\"Users can view their own roles\\"\n  ON public.user_roles\n  FOR SELECT\n  TO authenticated\n  USING (auth.uid() = user_id);\n\nCREATE POLICY \\"Admins can view all roles\\"\n  ON public.user_roles\n  FOR SELECT\n  TO authenticated\n  USING (public.has_role(auth.uid(), 'admin'));\n\nCREATE POLICY \\"Only admins can manage roles\\"\n  ON public.user_roles\n  FOR ALL\n  TO authenticated\n  USING (public.has_role(auth.uid(), 'admin'));\n\n-- Create function to update timestamps\nCREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION public.update_updated_at_column()\nRETURNS TRIGGER AS $$\nBEGIN\n  NEW.updated_at = now();\n  RETURN NEW;\nEND;\n$$ LANGUAGE plpgsql SET search_path = public;\n\n-- Create trigger for updating timestamps on profiles\nCREATE TRIGGER update_profiles_updated_at\n  BEFORE UPDATE ON public.profiles\n  FOR EACH ROW\n  EXECUTE FUNCTION public.update_updated_at_column();"}		gillsaabepicenterprise@gmail.com	\N

--
-- Name: objects objects_update_create_prefix; Type: TRIGGER; Schema: storage; Owner: supabase_storage_admin
--

CREATE TRIGGER objects_update_create_prefix BEFORE UPDATE ON storage.objects FOR EACH ROW WHEN (((new.name <> old.name) OR (new.bucket_id <> old.bucket_id))) EXECUTE FUNCTION storage.objects_update_prefix_trigger();

--

--
-- Name: policies Admins can manage all policies; Type: POLICY; Schema: public; Owner: postgres
--

CREATE POLICY "Admins can manage all policies" ON public.policies USING (public.has_role(auth.uid(), 'admin'::public.app_role));


--
-- Name: profiles Admins can view all profiles; Type: POLICY; Schema: public; Owner: postgres
--

CREATE POLICY "Admins can view all profiles" ON public.profiles FOR SELECT TO authenticated USING (public.has_role(auth.uid(), 'admin'::public.app_role));


--
-- Name: user_roles Admins can view all roles; Type: POLICY; Schema: public; Owner: postgres
--

CREATE POLICY "Admins can view all roles" ON public.user_roles FOR SELECT TO authenticated USING (public.has_role(auth.uid(), 'admin'::public.app_role));


--
-- Name: user_roles Only admins can manage roles; Type: POLICY; Schema: public; Owner: postgres
--

CREATE POLICY "Only admins can manage roles" ON public.user_roles TO authenticated USING (public.has_role(auth.uid(), 'admin'::public.app_role));


--
-- Name: policies Staff can view active policies; Type: POLICY; Schema: public; Owner: postgres
--

CREATE POLICY "Staff can view active policies" ON public.policies FOR SELECT USING ((public.has_role(auth.uid(), 'staff'::public.app_role) AND (status = 'active'::text)));


--
-- Name: profiles Users can update their own profile; Type: POLICY; Schema: public; Owner: postgres
--

CREATE POLICY "Users can update their own profile" ON public.profiles FOR UPDATE TO authenticated USING ((auth.uid() = user_id));


--
-- Name: profiles Users can view their own profile; Type: POLICY; Schema: public; Owner: postgres
--

CREATE POLICY "Users can view their own profile" ON public.profiles FOR SELECT TO authenticated USING ((auth.uid() = user_id));


--
-- Name: user_roles Users can view their own roles; Type: POLICY; Schema: public; Owner: postgres
--

CREATE POLICY "Users can view their own roles" ON public.user_roles FOR SELECT TO authenticated USING ((auth.uid() = user_id));
